Where are you boxing this weekend?

337 messages in this thread | Started on 2004-04-23

Where are you boxing this weekend?

From: fleurdelislb | Date: 2004-04-23 21:22:08 UTC
Since it's supposed to be a nice weekend (at least up this way),
we're planning on going out and getting our final Perkiomen Trail LB
tomorrow, and perhaps head over to Jersey on Sunday.

I will say, however, that I refuse to bike from Philly to the PT LB
since last time we did it was 50 miles round trip! We'll be parking
much closer to the box this time :p

I can't get enough of this spring weather! :)

FdL
http://fleurdelislb.blogspot.com

Re: [lbma] Where are you boxing this weekend?

From: Hikers_n_ Hounds | Date: 2004-04-23 21:53:27 UTC
I am going to Neshaminy State Park on Saturday to keep an eye on our Treasure Hunt boxes during the "Great PA Clean Up" and to do an exchange with Cyclonic. Sunday I may run down to Valley Garden Park in DE to check on the "Long Strange Trip" 'boxes as I got an email from a finder who advised that box #2 is wet inside, so I guess I need to do some repairs. If not, will try to hunt some of Raindeers boxes in PA.
 
Have a great weekend all and I am very sorry for my stupidity on posting on LBNA my email to ukletterboxer. It seems to have started yet another flame war. I think I am done with that list. But I was dumb and it was my error. Oh well,,,dragging our tails behind us...
 
Hikers & Hounds

Re: [lbma] Re: Where are you boxing this weekend?

From: Hikers_n_ Hounds | Date: 2004-04-24 00:12:02 UTC
I LOVE that park! The first and only time I have been there was at the Leap Day Gathering, which was SO much fun. The only drawback for me is the Hounds. They have very strict leash laws there and several trails I can't take my dogs on. And once we are way back in a trail I like to let mey dogs off leash to play. But when I was talking to a ranger there she said they really do fine people. so I will have to go back someday without my mutts. We found 3 boxes but never found the 4th! But what a beautiful place to go. Enjoy!!

I LOVE that park! The first and only time I have been there was at the Leap Day Gathering, which was SO much fun. The only drawback for me is the Hounds. They have very strict leash laws there and several trails I can't take my dogs on. And once we are way back in a trail I like to let mey dogs off leash to play. Re: [lbma] Where are you boxing this weekend?

From: Hikers_n_ Hounds | Date: 2004-04-24 01:05:38 UTC
Scarab,
 
I guess what I meant was I give up on that board because I do not seem to be serious enough for them. Mark, the guy who got upset, made some very good points. He has every right to feel the way he does. I am really enjoying letterboxing, but don't even count our finds or placements. I think we are about 5 or 6 finds and up to 10 plants, 4 of which are still waiting for us to post the clues. I honeslty would have asked for permission before I sent Andy anything, but I didn't think before I told him yes. He's a really nice guy and I think you would enjoy corresponding with him. You are very witty and literate and he seems to be as well. I think I am still smarting from a comment Ryan made on the list shortly after I posted that I was creating a postal letterbox. He and Steve Rayvenhouse were having a flame war over Steve's website and Ryan made a comment about not wanting to have to read all the mindless chatter about PLB's., etc. Then I sent this bonehead email today, oh well. So I think I am just not serious enough for the national board. Not that you folks aren't also serious about this hobby. But you sure are a lot of fun!!
 
I loved FdeL's post "Where are you boxing this weekend?". I thought that was great and hope she does it every Friday. Have a great weekend and I will try not to put my foot in my mouth anymore than I have done already. I'm looking forward to exchanging with Cyclonic tomorrow and hope to get down your way to hunt some boxes there too. I love to walk in Great Falls Park. I assume it's national so I can't plan to plant there but it just a great place to walk. I'll give you the heads up a couple of weeks before I head down.
 
Irene

were Girl Scouts on Steroids!LOL (no offense to the younger scouts
out there -- maybe I should get my old badge sash out (it wasn't all
that full) for displaying my first LB100 patch?!? First I have to
find another 98.

Hikers_n_ Hounds <hikers_n_hounds@...> wrote:
Scarab,
 
I guess what I meant was I give up on that board because I do not seem to be serious enough for them. Mark, the guy who got upset, made some very good points. He has every right to feel the way he does. I am really enjoying letterboxing, but don't even count our finds or placements. I think we are about 5 or 6 finds and up to 10 plants, 4 of which are still waiting for us to post the clues. I honeslty would have asked for permission before I sent Andy anything, but I didn't think before I told him yes. He's a really nice guy and I think you would enjoy corresponding with him. You are very witty and literate and he seems to be as well. I think I am still smarting from a comment Ryan made on the list shortly after I posted that I was creating a postal letterbox. He and Steve Rayvenhouse were having a flame war over Steve's website and Ryan made a comment about not wanting to have to read all the mindless chatter about PLB's., etc. Then I sent this bonehead email today, oh well. So I think I am just not serious enough for the national board. Not that you folks aren't also serious about this hobby. But you sure are a lot of fun!!
 
I loved FdeL's post "Where are you boxing this weekend?". I thought that was great and hope she does it every Friday. Have a great weekend and I will try not to put my foot in my mouth anymore than I have done already. I'm looking forward to exchanging with Cyclonic tomorrow and hope to get down your way to hunt some boxes there too. I love to walk in Great Falls Park. I assume it's national so I can't plan to plant there but it just a great place to walk. I'll give you the heads up a couple of weeks before I head down.
 
Irene

Re: Where are you boxing this weekend?

From: tempusfugitmd | Date: 2004-04-24 21:14:03 UTC
Hi, all!

My inlaws are visiting for my son's confirmation, so we don't have time to do actual letterboxing. However, Dead Duck Chuck and I did
get a hike in today to check on my Birder Series in Boyds, MD. All four are just fine (SCARAB, hint hint!) and to my surprise the logs
are filling up. I'm always happy to find my boxes safe and sound.

It was a beautiful day to be out of the house. We observed a loooong black snake and brought home a cool 4-point deer antler. I love
this hobby!

Donna in Maryland
aka Tempus Fugit

You silly ducks.  We were there today!  We rushed out on this first opportunity to get your new Cicada.  So now we have a page full of 5 beautiful stamps, Cicada and 4 birds. 
 
How few miles did you claim it was?  100 paces?  Is that Night Owl paces or Scarab paces?  There are  lot of deer trails and a lot pine trees around here.  Answer, finally, Scarab paces.  We spent a bit of time at the "first" set of cut logs along the trail.  But that's all part of the thrill of the hunt isn't it?

From: Hikers_n_ Hounds | Date: 2004-05-04 10:35:40 UTC
...and how many times will you ride the Pheonix while you are there? Before back surgery I was a roller coaster junkie too! Now I can only remeber what it's like. The Pheonix, even though it's small, was one of my favorites. And I only liked wooden coasters. None of that smooth metal upside down crap. Give me the clackety clack of a wooden roller coaster as it slowly reaches it's apex to the smooth, silent indifference of a metal coaster any day. My first husband and I went to Knoebels every year for 15 years and I can't count how many times I've ridden the Pheonix. Reading all of the Knoebel's posts brings back so many fond memories. One of my favorite places in the world.

Re: Where are you boxing this weekend?

From: Lightnin Bug | Date: 2004-06-12 21:34:55 UTC
Well, all baked, Thomas and I have finished our Saturday Morning
Letterbox crusade in Green Lane Park in the Perky Valley this
morning. We had much fun, boxing, playing with cicadas, inchworms
and whatever interests a 10 year old kid!

All told we found 7 Letterboxes (Red Maple, Yellow Oak and the 4 on
the Hemlock Point trail and the coveted Ruby Throat Hitchhiker)
before kid fatigue, the need to get Tom back home for his haircut at
his aunt's and my need to cut the lawn made us climb into the
econobox and mosey back to Allentown.

Funny, looking at the title of this post, I cant help think of people
in the "squared circle" getting ready to release fists of fury!

Anyway, for those of you in the Allentown area this weekend, there is
a Wine and Food Festival at Cedar Beach Park, just a stone's throw
from General Trexler's Letterbox. We'll be winos tomorrow, but
scouting for places to stash some boxes.

Have a great day.

Lightnin' Bug
F9 P4 HH1 (finally some non-pathetic stats!!)

[lbma] Re: Where are you boxing this weekend?

From: A. M. | Date: 2004-06-13 05:43:33 UTC
Took a trip into the Pines today. Didn't try for
Ssss! but found a mystery box and Oh, Be My Friend.
Of course, that last wasn't as manageable as it should
have been.

I had no problem getting to the location from the NW,
but once I was there I pulled my usual silliness and
forgot to read the end of the sentences in the
instructions. Does anyone else have this problem? I
just focus so much on part of an instruction that I
don't see the rest. Well...at least my fiance found
plenty to amuse him. (He doesn't indulge in
letterboxing himself.)

Anyway, I had a great time in the gorgeous weather.
The deer ticks weren't too numerous and the stamps
were well worth the trek. More people should visit Oh
Be My Friend. It's a fun box, and judging by the
logbook, unjustifiably lonely. :)

Of course I forgot to drop off the hitchhiker I
have...I'll have to run out this week and put that
somewhere. I doubt I'll be taking my poor Saturn over
dirt roads again soon. I don't want to abuse her too
much.

Hello Kitty

Glad to hear that you made it back! There're a couple of boxes that
I've been putting off looking for because I wasn't sure about the
condition of the roads. I've considered contacting the placer and

drive adventure only. After having found 2, however, I think that
that particular placer makes looking for boxes an adventure not a

that it wouldn't matter if I were boxing naked, cause I sure as heck
wasn't going to run into anyone else. OK, it was a weird thought but
weird thoughts pop into the minds of people standing alone in the
woods.

Re: Where are you boxing this weekend?

From: Hikers_n_ Hounds | Date: 2004-06-13 16:56:56 UTC
On Saturday H&H headed back up to Doylestown to hunt Celtic Cat's "Who is the Author" 6 box series. We expected to be in and out pretty quickly with 6 more boxes added to our Find count. I guess we are turning into real letterboxers after all, we've started counting. My friend Mike is our newest member and official navigator. Chapman Park was pretty easy to find and at first glance seems a tiny little park. It turned about to be a little bigger than we thought and was very charming. The hike was a lot of fun and the boxes were just great!!! I had an inkling who the auther was by the third box but still wasn't sure, and when the 6th box was opened I was thrilled to see that I guessed correctly! This was a great series and I sent Celtic Cat a big thank you.
 
I was going to plant my kids boxes in Tamenend Park today but a look around my house and I realized I really need to spend some time here. Oh well, I guess I have to act like a grown up every now and then!
 
Anyway, I hope everyone enjoyed the beautiful weekend and can't wait to hear what you all have been up to. I'm glad Fleur de Lis had such great camping weather! I hope we get as lucky in July.
 
Irene - H&H
F27 P10 X46

Re: Where are you boxing this weekend?

From: fleurdelislb | Date: 2004-06-14 00:15:10 UTC
--- In lbma@yahoogroups.com, Hikers_n_ Hounds <hikers_n_hounds@y...>
> Anyway, I hope everyone enjoyed the beautiful weekend and can't
wait to hear what you all have been up to. I'm glad Fleur de Lis had
such great camping weather! I hope we get as lucky in July.

Maybe it was great weather in SE Pa, but not so in Western PA! We
drove down on Friday, in pouring rain. We ended up checking into a
hotel on Friday b/c it was raining so hard that we couldn't set up
camp! However, around 8:30 pm the clouds cleared and we said to heck
with the hotel and went and set up camp via the car headlights :p It
rained again for about 2 hours last night. Our camp sight was a muddy
mess the whole time!

Ah well...I managed to plant an LB (still have to write up the
clues..should do that now in between loads of muddied laundry) so it
was worth it!

FdL

Re: [lbma] Re: Where are you boxing this weekend?

From: Cyclonic07@aol.com | Date: 2004-06-14 00:21:47 UTC
 
Well, seems like a lot of us got out this weekend, and why not, it was a perfect weekend for it. 
 
Yesterday, I also ventured to Green Lane, sorry I missed other folks that went.  When was everyone there?  I was in the park between 10 and 1. 
 
Anyways, I first ventured along the Hemlock Point trail and got all four boxes there.  Very nice stamps, and all boxes were in fine condition.
 
I next headed to the other side of the park and first went for the Golden Oak, and then Blue Butterfly.  I found Golden Oak easily, but it looks as if the Blue Butterfly has fluttered away.  I found the hiding spot, but only found an empty zip-lock bag :(
 
Disappointed, but not deterred, I searched for Green Tree Frog.  No problem there, it was found high and dry.  By this time I was out of gas, having not eaten yet, and headed out.
 
I was going to plant today, but I got stuck at home doing some work outside.  Next weekend I hope to plant a bunch of boxes for the July camping weekend :)

Nathan Brown
AKA Cyclonic

RE: [lbma] Where are you boxing this weekend?

From: Elizabeth Grace | Date: 2004-06-21 00:09:03 UTC
We made it to Green Lane Nature Center Saturday and found all four boxes there.  It was a beautiful hike!  I'm afraid to admit that it was nice looking for boxes that were on the easy side after our adventure at Nolde Forest. :)  My husband is hooked and my kids would rather go letterboxing than almost anything else.  This is great - I get to hike WITHOUT all the whining!  We also camped at Boulder Woods campground, not too far from Green Lane.
 
I think we're going to head back up there next weekend and finish the rest in Green Lane Park.  We ran out of water Saturday, so we went back to camp and swam, rather than continuing on as we'd planned.  Everyone is tired and tanned!
 
Thank you to everyone who responded to my question about Michaels.  I can say for sure that the stores in Willow Grove and by Montgomery Mall aren't carrying carving supplies any more.  I went back one more time, since I have a better idea of what I'm looking for now.  Guess I'll check out online! 
 
Its funny, this started out as a hobby to make hiking more fun for my kids by finding the boxes and now we all want to carve our own stamps!  So far, I've done one for each of my children, but they're pretty amateurish since I did them with an Exacto knife.
 
Happy Fathers' Day to all you dads out there!
 
Elizabeth
aka The Mama Fishy

Are you guys coming to the gathering July 9-11? We are camping at Colonial Woods in Upper Black Eddy, or for those who don't want to camp, there is a day gathering at the Sullivan Pavillion in Washington Crossing, right behind the Thompson Neely House on Saturday the 10 from 9-3. H&H

Elizabeth Grace <traininup3@...> wrote:
We made it to Green Lane Nature Center Saturday and found all four boxes there.  It was a beautiful hike!  I'm afraid to admit that it was nice looking for boxes that were on the easy side after our adventure at Nolde Forest. :)  My husband is hooked and my kids would rather go letterboxing than almost anything else.  This is great - I get to hike WITHOUT all the whining!  We also camped at Boulder Woods campground, not too far from Green Lane.
 
I think we're going to head back up there next weekend and finish the rest in Green Lane Park.  We ran out of water Saturday, so we went back to camp and swam, rather than continuing on as we'd planned.  Everyone is tired and tanned!
 
Thank you to everyone who responded to my question about Michaels.  I can say for sure that the stores in Willow Grove and by Montgomery Mall aren't carrying carving supplies any more.  I went back one more time, since I have a better idea of what I'm looking for now.  Guess I'll check out online! 
 
Its funny, this started out as a hobby to make hiking more fun for my kids by finding the boxes and now we all want to carve our own stamps!  So far, I've done one for each of my children, but they're pretty amateurish since I did them with an Exacto knife.
 
Happy Fathers' Day to all you dads out there!
 
Elizabeth
aka The Mama Fishy

I don't know if we'll be able to make it or not.  Our plans tend to be made at the last minute, so I'm never sure exactly where we'll be on a given weekend.  When it comes to camping, we watch the weather on Thursday & Friday before we decide to camp.  We have a great tent with one teensy problem - it leaks like a sieve.  It's no problem putting the a tarp over it for week-long trips, but its a real pain to rig it when we're only staying a night or two.  I just can't figure out why we didn't notice it was lacking a rain fly when we bought it...
 
At any rate, the gathering sounds like a lot of fun and we have so much to learn! 
 
Elizabeth

Where are you boxing this weekend?

From: Hikers_n_ Hounds | Date: 2004-07-16 11:53:44 UTC
I am flying north to New Hampshire this weekend to visit my childhood best friend who moved there about 3 years ago. I am introducing her and her family to this wonderful addiction and we are meeitng up with two area letterboxers. The only sad thing is that Dude the Wonder Dog can't go with me (stupid FAA regulations!) and he knows something is up because I haven't gone to work yet, am in my shorts and hiking sandals and have been fiddling with my backpack. He keeps whining and jumping thinking we are going boxing together. I'll have to make it up to him next weekend and box our brains out. 
 
I didn't get to do my grovelling thing on Tuesday. You may recall I am actually going to ask permission (!) to plant a series in Southampton Twp, Pa and had an appointment to appear before the Dept of Parks & Recreation on Tuesday the 13. Well, they called me and said they were going to have a quick 10 minute mini-meeting for their executive council only and can I please come in August instead. I will keep you posted. It's a great park, lot's of pretty trails and I have my 7 box children's series all ready to plant.  
 
Have a great weekend everyone and if anyone is looking for a trail buddy Dude is standing at the front door waiting to be rescued!
 
H&H

Re: Where are you boxing this weekend?

From: cahillymom | Date: 2004-07-16 22:00:10 UTC
Boxing. Ah yes, boxing. Well, I WAS going to check on a box of mine
this morning and go find one this afternoon, but a funny thing
happened on the trail. We were just strolling along, the daughter
and I, both in the wrong shoes, having not planned on hiking.
And there's a rabbit. No, no, Not the one that would have matched
the chipmunks and made sense along the trail. A WHITE rabbit, grey
spots. Calmly munching. Obviously abandoned. "Oooooooh," coos my
dear daughter. "Ah, but can you catch it?" says I. Off with the
shoes and into the underbrush she flies.
So, now the "free" rabbit is in an old hutch of my brother's and has
cost us $35 in supplies.
So, now to refocus...
Boxing.... must go boxing.....
Aud

Re: Where are you boxing this weekend?

From: sowbiz | Date: 2004-07-16 22:25:04 UTC
I was hoping to celebrate my BD with F100 but when I was clearing the
kitchen table I found two clue sheets with stamps on them (from when
I forgot my logbook one day) which means I already reached F100 with
HnH's Big Green Monster Box #2. At least it was a beautiful stamp
and I actually found this box - despite being with eagle eye Russ and
tenacious Sadie and fast walking Mary that day in PA when I was
generally a 'tag-a-long'.

If Sun isn't rainy I'll still take my mother (88) out for a 'box
lunch' - she'll treat me to lunch and I'll treat her to a letterbox.

At a staff meeting today I introduced my manager's manager to LB'g.
She is very excited since the family is going to RI in August.
Although I don't know how artistic they will be, since she asked me
to carve her trail stamp. Anything for a brownie point . . .
excluding hard work.

Judy B
Fairfax VA

the chipmunks and made sense along the trail. A WHITE rabbit, grey
spots. Calmly munching. Obviously abandoned. "Oooooooh," coos my
dear daughter. "Ah, but can you catch it?" says I. Off with the
shoes and into the underbrush she flies.
So, now the "free" rabbit is in an old hutch of my brother's and has
cost us $35 in supplies.
So, now to refocus...
Boxing.... must go boxing.....
Aud
***************************************************
AHHHHHHH!!!!!  Get the Holy Hand Grenade!!!  ;-)

Nathan Brown
AKA Cyclonic
***************************************************
 "Oh good, my dog found the chainsaw!"

Re: Where are you boxing this weekend?

From: Lightnin Bug | Date: 2004-08-06 23:01:54 UTC
Ah, Jerry Seinfeld's home town! 'pequa that is, Manhasset has the
Miracle Mile (ala Billy Joel).

LI has some things going against it from a letterboxing perspective -

1) It is mostly urban or suburban until you get out to Suffolk
County. Parks tend to be of the 'well manicured variety'.

2) LI is what was left behind after the last Ice Age ended. LI is
mostly sand, and you need to get up to the North Shore to see any
sort of rocks and old dead trees of any size. There are lots of nice
areas up in northern LI that would be perfect like Sagamore Hill,
Lloyd's neck and Garvie's point. Some ideas closer to 'pequa are
Massapequa preserve, Bethpage Park or Tackapawsha park.

There is the potential for microboxes, but even geocachers struggle
in the Guyland!

Lightnin' Bug

Report on Bucks County boxes

From: Silent Doug | Date: 2004-08-13 11:28:25 UTC
I took some time yesterday and logged a few more in Bucks County:

Flight of the Hawk
Sunrise Trek/Peace in the Valley
NPIV Compass Points
Henson's Friends
Kid's Castle
Jane Austen: Emma

I also found two hitchhikers, The Train and Stampy -- but unfortunately I
had already found both of them before! We're going to take them to boxes
somewhere out of PA so maybe that won't happen again. <g>

I was stumped by Delaware Valley College, since towards the end the clues
didn't really match up with the landscape (one marker listed as being on
the left wasn't, the number of rocks wasn't the same, the tree to look for
stood alone not near the next landmark, etc.). I would have searched more
for it, but was already feeling too conspicuous on the campus groups,
especially with workers busy mowing the lawns nearby. Then, as the clues
started to break away from what I was seeing, I had less and less
confidence that I was in the right place. Maybe when school's back in
session I'll try again.

Are Indigo Vulture and Muk-Luk on this group? I didn't think so, and I
invited them when I sent them a report on their boxes from the day's
quests. (The planters of the other boxes are already here, I'm pretty
sure.) I've been thinking how easy it would be if all the planters of boxes
in the area were on this group, then we could simply send reports to the
group instead of writing separately to each planter. Maybe as you all write
to letterboxers with reports from boxes in the region, you could invite
them to join the group if they're not already here, something like this:

>Also, the Letterboxing Mid-Atlantic discussion group is really going
>strong these days, with lots of talk about SE PA boxes in particular. If
>you're not on the list, maybe you should stop by!
>http://groups.yahoo.com/group/lbma/

Just a thought!

Doug

From: Silent Doug | Date: 2004-08-15 19:57:15 UTC
Jennifer and I logged 33 finds on Saturday (including one hitchhiker).

Of course, we had to go to Connecticut to do it!

:-)

We camped in SE CT and spent all day Saturday (or, at least, 11 hours of
the day, arriving in the first park at 8:30 am and wrapping up the last
letterbox at 7:30 pm). The weather was cooperative on Saturday, but turned
rainy Saturday night, so we came home early instead of trying to do any
more boxing on Sunday. (Yes, we have been known to letterbox in the rain,
but the thought of hiking in the rain and then facing a three-hour drive
home just wasn't so pleasant.)

We hit a good mix of 3-4 mile hikes, short walks and drive-by letterboxes,
including three series in the same park, with 5 boxes in each series, all
along a big loop on a half-dozen different trails. While a couple of the
boxes did require some diligent searching or retracing of steps, we did
eventually find all of the boxes that we tried for.

OK, I'm going back to drying out the tent and gear!

Doug

Re: not a bad day for letterboxing....

From: cahillymom | Date: 2004-08-15 20:35:17 UTC
> including three series in the same park, with 5 boxes in each
series, all
> along a big loop on a half-dozen different trails.

OK, technique question:
Do you keep shuffling through three clue sheets seeing what might
come up next, do the whole loop three times, or figure out on a map
ahead of time how the series overlap?
We did two series in one park once (only once, since this is not CT)
and had to pore over the map and then read one set of clues
backwards.
Aud

Re: [lbma] Re: not a bad day for letterboxing....

From: Silent Doug | Date: 2004-08-15 23:30:34 UTC
At 04:35 PM 8/15/2004, you wrote:
>OK, technique question:
>Do you keep shuffling through three clue sheets seeing what might
>come up next, do the whole loop three times, or figure out on a map
>ahead of time how the series overlap?
>We did two series in one park once (only once, since this is not CT)
>and had to pore over the map and then read one set of clues
>backwards.

All three were planted by the same person, and they weren't on the same
trails, but series #2 started at the end of series #1. When we finished #2,
we sat down, ate lunch and made a plan for #3. We figured out (correctly,
as it turned out) that we could probably pick up the trail for it nearby
without having to return to the car and drive to a new starting place, and
so we found them in the wrong order but with a lot less hiking than we
would have otherwise done.

In the past, when finding different series in the same park, we've had one
of us lead with one set of clues while the other pays attention to the
other looking for common landmarks. Usually I've found that it's nearly
impossible for me (when I'm letterboxing alone) to keep in mind parts of
other clues that are in the same park, since I can only really concentrate
on one thing at a time. However, last week when I found the 5 boxes in
Peace Valley, I did read them all beforehand and mark their approximate
locations on a map of the park, and that saved a lot of walking on the same
trails. Many clues don't lend themselves to this, either, since you don't
get enough detail on the specific locations of the boxes just from the
clues. But I always try to plan ahead so that I don't finish finding a
letterbox and only then realize that I walked past one on the way (which
has happened more times than I care to remember!)

silentdoug@...

>Go past the granite marker with a red arrow, across the railroad
>tracks, alongside the stone wall, across the road, down the winding
>dirt path, around the boulder on the right, up to the pine tree. Reach
>into the hole in the rotting log nearby and Bingo! There it is, a
>little Tupperware container.
>
>On the lid is written "This is not trash! This is a letterbox."
>
>Letterboxing is like treasure hunting for a treasure with no intrinsic
>value. The idea is to follow clues posted on the Internet (which range
>from easy to diabolically hard) and find boxes that other letterboxers
>have hidden. It's a small but rapidly growing subculture of hobbyists
>in metro Atlanta and scattered worldwide, who sing the praises of
>hiking outdoors, participating as a family and solving a puzzle.
>
>"You get exercise. You get a nice view. You complete a quest," says
>Mark Britt, 32, of Stone Mountain.
>
>"My husband calls it hiking with purpose," says Beverly Matoney, who
>home schools her two children in Alpharetta. "I'd get out and walk in
>the woods anyway, but this is a treasure at the end of a hike. It's
>definitely something for the whole family."
>
>Britt and Matoney will be among the first gathering of letterboxers in
>Georgia today at Stone Mountain Park. More than 50 letterboxers from
>nine states are expected to attend, and they'll be scouring the park
>for the 10 boxes hidden there. More than 100 letterboxes are hidden
>around Georgia, from one near the Newton County Courthouse in
>Covington to one near Emory University. But Stone Mountain Park has
>the highest concentration of letterboxes in the state.
>
>Most of the people attending the gathering have never met but have
>corresponded through e-mail. Although letterboxing itself is a
>somewhat solitary pursuit, hobbyists connect on the Internet,
>sometimes forming online communties in places like Yahoo Groups.
>
>"This might not exist if not for the Internet," says Britt, who edits
>catalogs for an automotive restoration company but calls letterboxing
>"almost like a second job, but one you don't get paid for."
>
>Letterboxing is about more than hunting. Most letterboxers create
>their own hand-carved rubber stamps (some buy them in stores, but
>that's considered less classy) and make their own personalized
>logbooks. When a box is found, it will have its own unique stamp and
>book inside. The finder prints his or her own personal stamp into the
>box's book, then adds the stamp from the box to his or her logbook.
>Then the box is resealed and carefully returned to its hiding place
>for the next person to find.
>
>Leafing through a letterbox's book, which may be the size of a deck of
>cards or a paperback book, reveals a history of everyone who has been
>there, using their "trail names": Silent Doug, She Who Plants, Poison
>Ivy, Psycho Mommy, Amyrica, Town Crier. Some homemade stamps are
>simple; some are like little masterpieces of folk art.
>
>There's no competition in letterboxing per se, but there is certainly
>prestige for finding or planting lots of boxes. Finding 100 boxes is
>generally considered a milestone.
>
>"Some people are famous, because they've found so many boxes," says
>Mike Fairman, a Salvation Army administrator from Loganville. "When
>you see a stamp like 'Wanda & Pete,' it's like seeing an autograph of
>someone famous."
>
>Fairman and his family's immersion into letterboxing is typical. He
>and his wife, Carol, heard about the activity in late December. Three
>days later, they tramped through more than 11 miles of trails in Stone
>Mountain Park, collecting and stamping.
>
>"We were hooked," says Carol Fairman. "At 35, I never would have seen
>myself running through a cornfield to get a stamp."
>
>Letterboxing is said to have begun in 1854, when James Perrott hid his
>calling card in a bottle near a pool in Devon, England, inviting
>others to add their cards. Eventually, people began leaving postcards
>("letterbox" is the British word for our "mailbox"), although there
>appears to be a long interval between Perrott and the revival of
>letterboxing in England in the 1980s and '90s. An article in
>Smithsonian Magazine in 1998 seems to have jumped letterboxing to
>North America, and while the Northeast and Pacific Northwest regions
>were stronger at first, now the South is playing catch-up.
>
>Unlike many activities, letterboxing has no organization or
>association. There are no rules, although there is a system of
>etiquette that includes caring for other people's boxes and not
>damaging nature.
>
>As a result, there's no way to know how many people are into
>letterboxing. Britt guesses there might be no more than 100 in metro
>Atlanta, but the number of boxes and hunters is growing rapidly.
>
>"In January, there were 38 letterboxes in Georgia, and now there's
>over 100," says Britt.
>
>There's a fair amount of ambivalence about the activity becoming
>widespread and attracting masses of new hunters because of the respect
>and care needed to protect the system of hiding and finding.
>
>"It's starting to really blow up," says Fairman. "When it's a small
>number of people, you can trust them. But the more people you have,
>the less trust you have."
>
>GETTING STARTED WITH LETTERBOXING ON THE WEB
>The main North American site:
><http://www.letterboxing.org>www.letterboxing.org
>Another main portal: <http://www.atlasquest.com>www.atlasquest.com
>A list of Georgia letterboxes:
>www.letterboxing.orgBoxByRegion.asp?region=Georgia
>"The Letterboxer's Companion" by Randy Hall (Falcon, $14.95), a book
>about the hobby:
><http://www.amazon.com/exec/obidosASIN0762727942/douglasgerlach/104-0187364-7542364>www.amazon.com/exec/obidosASIN0762727942/douglasgerlach/104-0187364-7542364
>



|-#-#-#-#-#-#-#-#-#-#-#-#-#-#-#-#-#-#-|
Silent Doug, P38 F440 X72 E10
silentdoug@...
http://www.letterboxing.info

RE: [lbma] Rain Rats!: Where are you boxing this weekend?

From: Kathryn Wolfe | Date: 2004-08-23 15:05:07 UTC
    Well, all the rain kept us from Delaware this weekend -- pity.  But I did manage to pick up a few stamps nonetheless!  Searched for It's a Holiday (bunny stamp) -- after waiting nearby for several mallgoers to vacate the bench, found it alive and well in Pentagon City.  Also found A Flower for Mildred, which has such a great sentiment, and really enjoyed roaming the fort reading about the earthenworks.  Amazing to think that all of that would've been done by hand -- no mechanized earthmovers back then.
 
    Also went searching for Inlingua but unfortunately came up empty.  The second "There is no more Overlook" sign noted in the clues has been removed, but it was clear where it should've been, so following the trail wasn't a big deal.  We were sure that we found the proper place behind the tree, but no box.  Darn!  On the plus side, some birdwatchers we passed on the trail showed us a woodpecker way up high.
 
Hope your weekend was good,
 
Longhorn

Report: Nottingham, Ft. Washington boxes

From: Silent Doug | Date: 2004-09-18 22:20:33 UTC
Despite the rain, Jennifer and I found the Tastiest Tour on Earth today
while driving through Chester County on other business. We were accosted by
security, but they left us after a brief explanation. We were the first
finders, and also picked up the Run Like the Deer Hitchhiker in the box.

shape, though the park was really flooded in parts.

report: Media, Ambler & Blue Bell

From: Silent Doug | Date: 2004-09-22 13:42:59 UTC
Jennifer and I found these boxes on Sunday:

Early American Farm and Rose Tree in Media
B & E's First Box, Jumping Logs and Hummin' Bird in Ambler/Blue Bell

All were in good shape, though several had moisture inside because of
containers that weren't quite watertight. The contents of all were fine,
though we added some zip lock bags to several to add some additional
protection.

(Double bagging is really important if you want to keep letterbox contents
dry!)

From: gerania93 | Date: 2004-10-02 16:36:38 UTC
My weekend boxing came early. Yesterday on yet another trip up the
NE Ext. PA turnpike I was able to swoop into Nockamixon and pick up 2
more boxes - LOTR One Ring and Catch the Wind. One Ring was a bit
damp, generally in good shape though the box wasn't covered when I
found it. Catch the Wind needed a little more care but the log was
dry. I'm sorry to report that a piece was broken off of the stamp but
it is still usable.

Re: [lbma] Re: Where are you boxing this weekend?

From: Cyclonic07@aol.com | Date: 2004-10-03 00:05:02 UTC
In a message dated 10/2/2004 7:33:41 AM Eastern Standard Time, rpboehme@... writes:
Cyclonic and I may be joined by Cichlid Guy and Team Rabbit to hunt
for some elusive mystery boxes in Berks County.

Lightnin' Bug
 
***************************************************
And what a successful day we had!  No rain, well, a little drizzle, hardly noticeable.
 
Lightnin' Bug and I meet at about 11 and set out for Mad Hatter's HHH.  I showed him the shortcut there and then allowed him to find it with the clues (and I didn't even have to say if he was getting warmer;-) ).
 
We then waited at the car while Cichlid Guy and Team Rabbit meet up with us.  Very nice people and baby rabbit is a cutie.  CG has soon really outstanding carvings, a very nice stamp and a great traveler.  Team Rabbit's personal stamps were fantastic as well.  Baby rabbit has her own log, and it is already almost full!
 
After heading back to the HHH again so the newcomers could get it, we headed out for Homage, and found it easily.  Another nice stamp.
 
Cichlid Guy and Team Rabbit had to split, so LB and I headed off to find Mobius Trip, which we did.  Not too many finders for this box.  I think we are slowly getting all of the Berks area boxes, many of them are mysteries, so I am pretty happy about that.  Guess I have to get out and plant some more :-)


Nathan Brown
AKA Cyclonic
***************************************************
 "Oh good, my dog found the chainsaw!"

Re: Where are you boxing this weekend?

From: Lightnin Bug | Date: 2004-10-03 00:15:51 UTC
Thanks for the kind words. The pleasure was mine, and I am glad that
the rain petered out! One thing I can say is that today all of the
skeeters in PA must have been there waiting for us.

The HHH was cool, Homage was spotted from the trail and Cyclonic and
I had an interesting time tracking down the Mobius (S)Trip - very
cool stamps all around.

Of course, these boxes are in undisclosed locations!

There was mass hitchhiker exchanging with Klingons being destined for
Michigan along with an Indiana sailboat and some protozoans heading
somewhere. The A-meba and Paramecium are on the move one will be in
PA and the other in Michigan, I theeenk! The Euglena will eventually
end up in the South Mountain HHH, to restock the box (hey, you need
to leave one to take one!!).

Tiredly typing,

Lightnin' Bug

Well, today looks like it's going to be a perfect day
to box but I have a funeral this morning, not a family
member for a change! So that will tie up my morning
and afternoon. Dude and I wanted to finish the Ben
Frankling boxes. If I get home early enouhg I may
boogie up to Pennypack and grab 'em. Also, a new boxer
should be joing this list shortly. His name is Joseph.
He contacted me through the contact the placer
function as he was having trouble posting clues. He
eventually figured it out but we have been
corresponding. He lives in NE Philly and just planted
3 boxes in Pennypack as well. He wasn't aware of the
talk lists and missed the gathering so I told him to
hurry up and join and we would give him a rousing
welcome! Keep an eye out for his post.

Sunday Dude and I are hoping to get our last Jane
Austin box, I have really enjoyed that series, meet up
with Eagle Bob to return his glasses and then plant a
couple of boxes in Tyler so that folks will have
something to hunt during Plantapalooza. We might try
to find a Muk-luk box that we couldn't find in the
spring if we have time after planting.

I guess I have some household chores or food shopping
to do but that is low on my priority list, plus Dude
doesn't like to do that stuff!

Re: Where are you boxing this weekend?

From: Jan | Date: 2004-10-24 21:26:58 UTC
Little dog, Barney, and I had a pretty successful letterboxing
weekend. We started out by planting our box in Tyler State Park for
the Plantapalooza Battle of the Bands and from there went to Delaware
Valley College where we found the Igpay Atinlay box on an absolutely
beautiful campus. We weren't as successful with the Alma Mater DVC
box. I think it is there, we just did something wrong and ended up
giving up on it. From there we accidentally ran into Chapman Park
and the "Who's the Author" series. Good old Mapquest couldn't give
us
directions to this park but we found it by driving around and were
very glad that we did. It was a great series and I am happy to say,
I figured out the author when I saw box number 5.

Today we headed to the John Fries Rebellion box in Trumbauersville.
I was focused so hard on following the clues that I wasn't really
paying a lot of attention to where we were walking. After we found
the box, which is back in the woods with very faint paths, thanks to
the fallen leaves, I looked around and wondered how we were going to
get back out. Well, I was happy to discover, that little empty
headed Barney has a talent for retracing a trail. He confidently led
us back out of the woods and I was rather amazed. Oh, yes, we picked
up a hitchhiker there so it was really rewarding.

After that we headed up to Nockamixon and found the Hungry Termites
before they make their trip out of state and the last two Lord of the
Rings boxes that we didn't have time to get last time we were there.
We also picked up the Blue Heron and the Jump for Joy boxes while we
were there. All in all, a happily successful weekend for us.

Jan and Barney now aka Team Little Dog

about the Delaware Canal

From: Silent Doug | Date: 2004-10-24 22:06:56 UTC
You may know that the Delaware Canal suffered severe damage during the
recent flooding, as I was reminded in this article today:
http://www.phillyburbs.com/pb-dyn/news/111-10242004-388601.html

Since there are a number of letterboxes hidden along the canal, you should
know that much of the canal towpath is closed and/or impassable.

Re: [lbma] about the Delaware Canal

From: Silent Doug | Date: 2004-10-25 00:19:45 UTC
At 07:55 PM 10/24/2004, you wrote:

>Last weekend 10/17 we came back from Nockamixon on 611 East and then took
>32 South to the Flemington/Frenchtown Bridge. The entire canal was empty
>up in that area. It really surprised us as we expected to see it
>overflowing. Why was that?

The canal isn't naturally filled with water -- there are valves and gates
and other mechanisms that control the flow of water into and out of the
canal. The flood caused three major breaks between the towpath and the
Delaware River, so the canal can't hold water -- and so no water is being
released into the canal.

There are photos and more information about the flood damage here:
http://www.fodc.org/



|-#-#-#-#-#-#-#-#-#-#-#-#-#-#-#-#-#-#-|
Silent Doug, P42 F568 X91 E12
silentdoug@...
http://www.letterboxing.info

Re: about the Delaware Canal

From: cahillymom | Date: 2004-10-25 12:57:17 UTC
For any avid Delaware Canal fans - There's a children's book, "A
tune for the towpath" by Jane Flory, which is set in New Hope. It
gives a great overview of life on the canal in its heyday, and the
illustrator obviously did the work on site. I find children's
fiction a great, quick-and-dirty way to learn the basics on a
variety of topics.
Aud

RE: [lbma] Re: Where are you boxing this weekend?

From: Myke Scholtes | Date: 2004-10-25 18:57:09 UTC
Message
I had a great letterboxing weekend.
 
On Saturday, I traveled through the 'Hamptons of Bucks County to find:
 
Tamanend Series
Brave Little Caterpillar Series
Branching Out
 
All boxes were in great shape, except I could not find Caterpillar # 4.  I found the hitchhiker Mesinholikan Mask in Branching Out.
 
Today, I did a little tour of Lightnin' Bug Country (also known as Lehigh County).  I found:
 
South Mountain Series
Rodale Fitness Park
Kalmbach Memorial Park
 
While all boxes are in good shape, there are some trail problems (flood-related, I imagine) to both Rodale and Kalmbach.  Obviously, one can still find the boxes, but I'll be letting Lightnin' Bug know specifics of the problems off list.  I picked up the Blivet HH at the South Mountain H^3.
 
Oh, and I have a new trail stamp.  It's kind of an homage to both my previous stamp and my trail name.  You'll have to find a box I've stamped in, or run into me on the trail, to see it.  :)
 
Peace,
Myke
"Indigo Vulture"

Re: [lbma] Where are you boxing this weekend?

From: Cyclonic07@aol.com | Date: 2004-10-26 00:03:20 UTC
 
I was not going to do any boxing this weekend, but as it turns out, I managed to get five boxes in.
 
Late Friday, Farmer Brown, Tommcat and I went out and found "Bolts and Holes" in the dark.  It was...interesting...to say the least.  The boxes were in fine shape.
 
Sunday, I was headed over to Clementon to do some coaster riding (had a free pass), and decided to stop at Palmyra Cove.  There were still some boxes I had yet to get, so I managed to quickly finish up the Pirate series.  All those were in fine shape as well.  One thing, are those boxes staying, or are they getting removed.  I was lucky to still have the clues buried in my car, because they are not online.

Re: Where are you boxing this weekend?

From: Jan | Date: 2004-10-30 22:08:20 UTC
The newly named Team Little Dog just got home from doing the
Arendtsville Wetlands in Adams County, and the Four Two Two and the
Mary Ann Furnace boxes at Codorus State Park in York County. We
started out the day at the Governor Dick tower and after walking the
mile and a half up the mountain, discovered that we forgot the
compass and were unable to find the box without it. How silly was
that!

Tomorrow we are heading out again - gotta make hay while the sun
shines - or in boxers terms, gotta get the stamps before they freeze
in the ground.

Janila and Barney of Team Little Dog

Re: Where are you boxing this weekend?

From: cahillymom | Date: 2004-10-31 01:01:57 UTC
Just got in from a 4 box day. We returned to the scene our
adventures of last weekend, and checked the correct side of the road
this time, nabbing the Pine Barrens Tree Frog. Marvelous carving,
interesting site. The guys want to go back after hunting season ends
to look for the plane wreckage. Picked up Sssssss also. And,
although my numbers were still way off on Southbound, we still
managed to get both What Exit? boxes along the way.
We checked our Pasadena boxes while down that way, and found that
the whole area is really suffering from party trash. There was a
state forest guy there writing a report when we arrived. I'm adding
trash bags to my "what's in your" bag. Someone had gathered four of
five bagloads of trash -- but then left them there for critters to
tear open and scatter! What a sad mess.
Any word from MGers yet?
Aud

All were in good or very good shape.

Re: Where are you boxing this weekend?

From: hexacat | Date: 2004-12-06 17:26:58 UTC
i'm glad the database is on your "to-do list" :) before you start the
arduous task of inputting your letterboxes make sure you download the
latest version (1.5)

this version allows the user to customize a print label order for
your postal letterboxes. everything else is pretty much the same.
oh, thanks to Silent Doug's idea i added a Find:Plant ratio under the
stats module. FYI: low ratio number = good!

happy holidays folks.
my nose is buried in engineering books for finals week. no play for
me. although i did manage to plant two more boxes yesterday. still
working on the clues. hopefully will post them sometime this week.

-hexacat

Re: Where are you boxing this weekend?

From: The Doubtful Guests | Date: 2005-01-18 00:36:24 UTC
It is 20 degrees here and I spent the last two days boxing with Wanda.  Did you know those hot hand chemical packs really work?  Did not notice the cold much. 
 
I am collecting Heist Trolls.  Jem Heist appears to be working on a troll series which are really fun.  Got three so far from across Nern VA.  His Beatles series at Lake Accotink was really fun too.  They were fun to color.  Wanda was glad to see they were fun stamps inspired by their songs, since she has a few images of them already.  Well I only have one Beatles image and it's a really good one.  Naturally I like beattles.
 
In two days we found:
 
Puddle Duck - in McLean
Vince Foster - in Mclean / Arlington
The Far Side of the Moo series on the Far Side - Turkey Run Park, McLean
Difficult Rock Troll - Great Falls
Paws for Thought - Great Falls
Leather and Metal series - Great Falls
Deerlick - Deerlick Park, Springfield
Lion, Witch, and Wardrobe - only found the Witch - Lake Accotink, Springfield
Accotink Bridge Troll - Lake Accotink, Springfield
A tribute to the Beatles series - Lake Accotink, Springfield
O&A RR - Lake Accotink, Springfield
Audobon series - Reston
Walker Bridge Troll - Reston
Audobon 2 series - Reston
Christmas Tree Graveyards - Reston
 
Scarab of the Doubtful Guests

Re: [lbma] Where are you boxing this weekend?

From: Samuel Checker | Date: 2007-06-11 13:54:06 UTC
We hit the Goshen Trail yestermorn, for an easy one (Fox Catcher). Daughter Number 1 is at an awkward age; she doesn't want to ride in the backpack but she doesn't want to walk more than a mile or so. So we put Daughter Number 2 in the backpack, which meant that Daughter Number 1 wanted to ride after half a mile.

(I'm looking on eBay for a second backpack carrier...)

But we found the box, Daughter Number 1 had good fun playing with the stamps and logbook, and we hiked the whole trail which meant we at least got a 2 mile walk in this weekend to go with the full day of weeding and window washing.

On 6/8/07, pamela cannon <momma22and2@...> wrote:

Re: Where are you boxing this weekend?

From: midlandtrailblazer | Date: 2007-06-12 12:20:51 UTC
We went out to our family cabin this weekend. Hubby, DS and I left
Thursday evening so that we could get up early Friday and go out
hunting. Found 5 boxes -- two at the Greenbrier River Trail in
Anthony, one at Blue Bend park (good hike!) then we dipped over into
VA for the I-64 Welcome Center box and the 2 Brothers box in Hot
Springs. We looked for the box at Humpback Bridge, because a note
on AQ said it needed TLC (a new logbook) but we couldn't find it.
Actually, hubby had had his limit -- he had already gotten into
poison ivy twice hunting the boxes in Anthony and had to "detox"
with jewelweed nearby. The bridge box, if we were looking in the
right place, was covered with PI. Instead we walked across the
bridge at the request of DS. By this time it was around 2:30, the
natives were getting restless, my mother and brother were at the
cabin and Mom would be making pizza in another hour, so I skipped
looking for the other two boxes I had clues for and we just went
home. DS fell asleep on the way back (he had a bit of a cold, so I
think he just wasn't feeling that great.)

Then, on the way home, we went through Fayetteville and the New
River Gorge to find 4 more boxes. We came home via Mossy to go
through Plum Orchard WMA and look for one, but that one seemed to be
MIA. The last person to look for it before us had also reported it
MIA. I know that doesn't always mean anything, because we went out
looking for the Red Rock box in Winfield a couple weeks ago that had
been reported MIA and we found it.

Even though we didn't find every box, and we didn't even hunt for
every box I had clues for, it was a good weekend and I finally got a
ribbon beside my name at AQ!!

Now I'm planning the next excursion....

midlandtrailblazer

Where are you boxing this weekend?

From: Nathan Brown | Date: 2009-11-15 02:50:53 UTC
Well, haven't heard the question in a while, so figured I would pose it,
where are you boxing this weekend?

Schizokeet and I headed down towards Fredericksburg. We succeeded in
finding a mystery box we were looking for, and afterwards found the
Neverland series which was a nice, short walk. We also visited a few of
the historic sites in the area and had a late lunch in Fredericksburg.
It was nice to get out, even though the sun never really peeked out, at
least it was not raining.

Tomorrow promises to be a nicer day, and we will be planting tomorrow up
in this area. Have a few boxes that need to get out and just discovered
a nice park nearby.

Next weekend is the last camping trip of the year, up to Caledonia State
Park in Pennsylvania. It is Rememberence Day in Gettysburg, so we plan
to see the parade, do some hiking, and finally plant some boxes out
there. Oh, and find a few too ;-)

--
Nathan Brown

AKA Cyclonic
Penncoasters.com

The Insensitivity rolls on...

Behind every great man is a great woman rolling her eyes

----- Original Message -----
From: Nathan Brown
To: lbma@yahoogroups.com
Sent: Saturday, November 14, 2009 9:50 PM
Subject: [lbma] Where are you boxing this weekend?

 

Well, haven't heard the question in a while, so figured I would pose it,
where are you boxing this weekend?

Schizokeet and I headed down towards Fredericksburg. We succeeded in
finding a mystery box we were looking for, and afterwards found the
Neverland series which was a nice, short walk. We also visited a few of
the historic sites in the area and had a late lunch in Fredericksburg.
It was nice to get out, even though the sun never really peeked out, at
least it was not raining.

Tomorrow promises to be a nicer day, and we will be planting tomorrow up
in this area. Have a few boxes that need to get out and just discovered
a nice park nearby.

Next weekend is the last camping trip of the year, up to Caledonia State
Park in Pennsylvania. It is Rememberence Day in Gettysburg, so we plan
to see the parade, do some hiking, and finally plant some boxes out
there. Oh, and find a few too ;-)

--
Nathan Brown

AKA Cyclonic
Penncoasters. com

The Insensitivity rolls on...

Where are you boxing this weekend?

From: Wisconsin Hiker | Date: 2010-04-18 00:42:25 UTC
I figured since we are IN the Mid-Atlantic region this weekend (Virginia), I could officially post the question!

We started yesterday in a park in Richmond, then had a very nice hike in the Wintergreen ski resort area. The trails were better than we expected and we found the Old Crow box that was planted in 2003 and stil had the original logbook in the box. Later in the after we tried for the Ultra 2 box with no success.

This morning we hiked in Douthat State Park and found Scarab's box at Blue Suck Falls. It's a very nice park and seems well suited for a gathering since it has camping AND cabins AND a prety extensive trail system that could certainly use some more boxes.

This afternoon we took the Belfast trail up to the Devil's Marble Yard. My, oh my! That was a challenging boulder scramble!!! We were happy to find the box, since searching in a rock field normally gives us trouble and were a bit surprised to discover that we were the first finders.

Tomorrow we're hoping to do two noydb boxes. Our plan is to try "Time to Stomp Some Waffles" (7 miles, 1,000 ft) in the morning, and then "Grinch Mountain" (6 miles, 1,700 ft) in the afternoon. If anyone is in the Roanoke area and wants to join us for one or both of these, let us know!

Wisconsin Hiker & Martini Man

Re: [lbma] Where are you boxing this weekend?

From: Randy Hall | Date: 2010-04-18 01:17:25 UTC

Yes, very nice park. Sounds like you had some great hikes.

Re: [lbma] Where are you boxing this weekend?

From: Otis' Friends | Date: 2010-04-18 14:10:33 UTC
Ambitious!
 
The 4 5/6 year old and I tackled the Cove Mountain Hawk Rock Loop (8.2 miles, 900 feet up) yesterday and finished it in less than 6.5 hours (counting boxing, lunch, a wrong turn, and trying to warm up at the shelter), which is pretty good for us.  Nice view from Hawk Rock and good letterboxing to be had along the trail.  Ran into over a dozen trail volunteers wrapping up at the shelter.

Re: [lbma] Where are you boxing this weekend?

From: kotlarek@wi.rr.com | Date: 2010-04-19 02:10:51 UTC
Yes, it WAS an ambitious plan, but we DID IT! Martini Man was quoting the Bug on our way down from the afternoon hike - "My dogs are barkin!". In addition, our knees were squealing and MM's hips were howling. It was great to hit the hot tub at the hotel tonight!

We did the McAfee Knob hike in a little under 4 hours, with time for photos & stamping in (roundtrip 7.4 miles). We were the first to visit it, possibly because the sign mentioned in the clues is gone. However the clever Martini Man spotted a bolt in a tree and then the remains of what we think might have been a sign in the underbrush. The box was placed in AUG 2008, so it was good that it finally had a visitor. Spectacular rock ledges and views from this spot on the AT (rumored to be the most scenic spot on the trail in VA).

The afternoon hike was MUCH more challenging! Quite a bit of straight up, STEEP elevation gain! Of course we forgot to pack our hiking poles. For some reason we often forget about them when heading east, but never forget them when heading west. However I had found a good natural stick on Friday that I am keeping for our trip. The climb today however required TWO sticks, so I harvested another from some deadfall along the trail. MM also acquired two sticks to assist in his ascent and descent. The hike was longer than advertised, I think because the trail was rerouted. It turned out to be 7.2 miles and took nearly 4.5 hours. Again a ton of wildflowers and flowering trees as well as numerous different types of butterflies. The trail at the top was VERY close to the Tinker Cliff dropoffs, so a bit nervewracking for me. We were third to visit this box, also planted in AUG 2008.

We hope we're not too stiff tomorrow to do the hike we planned - an 8-mile round trip hike to the highest point in VA....

Wisconsin Hiker

P.S. I hope you are not still carrying that girl! But if you're not - that is a good little hiker you've trained there! Has it been cold? We've been out in shorts & t-shirts every day down here (but started out w/some fleece jackets in the early morning).

Re: Where are you boxing this weekend?

From: top_hat_boxr | Date: 2010-04-21 22:24:25 UTC
Last weekend the RedHatBox'rs were boxing Rehoboth Beach DE -- completing their logistics for "Who Let the Dawgs Out" -- coming up April 16, 2011. AQ Details have been updated.

It wasn't all booze and banter -- we also knocked off two local DE Trail Challenge hikes.

Now as long as I don't lose my notes we should be good to roll.

I'll be updating the status of Lower Slower Swagger boxes -- esp after the boardwalk was wiped out and has been mostly rebuilt. Pink and her many eyes found the previously reported missing Larry -- lounging in the bushes right where he had landed. But the flat pouch is hard to spot.

THB'r

Where are you boxing this weekend?

From: Nathan Brown | Date: 2010-07-29 22:51:22 UTC
Whether is starting to look pretty bearable this weekend, which is good
since we have some outdoor plans.

Since we were thwarted by crowds, shopping and dinner in Gettysburg a
few weeks ago, we decided to return and go looking for some buttons.
Many boxes that were in Gettysburg, on the battlefield, are now gone.
Looks like the park did some pulling. However, my single box was still
well and in place as of the 10th. Penelope may get replaced, though in
a different spot, this weekend as well.

From there were are headed to Lancaster for some fun the rest of the
weekend. We are camping in Intercourse. While there I plan to replace
Goat Path Expressway and maybe toss out a few new clue cards ;-) Maybe
Sunday we will go searching for some mermaids.

So, what else is everyone doing this weekend?

--
Nathan Brown

AKA Cyclonic
Penncoasters.com
